  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_515c828c-3002-4de2-a788-bbbfea16d58a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText4414775843597151439" style="display:none">Everyone knows that Colin Bridgerton is the most charming man in London. Penelope Featherington has secretly adored her best friend's brother for...well, it feels like forever. After half a lifetime of watching Colin Bridgerton from afar, she thinks she knows everything about him, until she stumbles across his deepest secret...and fears she doesn't know him at all.<br /><br />Colin Bridgerton is tired of being thought nothing but an empty-headed charmer, tired of everyone's preoccupation with the notorious gossip columnist Lady Whistledown, who can't seem to publish an edition without mentioning him in the first paragraph. But when Colin returns to London from a trip abroad he discovers nothing in his life is quite the same - especially Penelope Featherington! The girl haunting his dreams. But when he discovers that Penelope has secrets of her own, this elusive bachelor must decide...is she his biggest threat - or his promise of a happy ending?</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2632188827" />
    <a title="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession"><img alt="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511556834p2/28967089.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2632188827?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" href="/user/show/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession">Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2632188827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14243292276037404720">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Though I loved Penelope Featherington, Colin was another story altogether. Before this book I really loved Colin. I couldn't wait for his story. Maybe my expectations were too high. I don't know but I really didn't like Colin most of the time. At times he came off like a big asshole. He was blowing his top every time the wind blew. His temper was just a bit much. One minute he was fine and then he was pissy, cold, and rude. If I was Penelope I would have kicked him in the balls. Penelop</span>
  <span id="freeText14243292276037404720" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />Though I loved Penelope Featherington, Colin was another story altogether. Before this book I really loved Colin. I couldn't wait for his story. Maybe my expectations were too high. I don't know but I really didn't like Colin most of the time. At times he came off like a big asshole. He was blowing his top every time the wind blew. His temper was just a bit much. One minute he was fine and then he was pissy, cold, and rude. If I was Penelope I would have kicked him in the balls. Penelope was sweet and smart. I felt bad that after being the shy wallflower that everyone acted like was a ugly plain girl, to have the man of your dream finally want you, only to have him snapping at you at the drop of a hat was just sad. Overall with the plot and Penelope this book was still 3 to 3.5 star read but Colin was a real disappointment. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14243292276037404720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">All romance fans &amp; readers who love stories where the unpopular heroine gets the guy!</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52574635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13939008361473153232"><i>Re-read/listened to the audiobook version Oct'2018</i>:<br/><br/>5 stars – Historical/Regency Romance<br/><br/>The audiobook narrator was fabulous, and it's still a big 5-star read for me.<br/><br/><i>Original Review from Sept'2010</i>: <br/><br/>5+ stars – Historical/Regency Romance <br/><br/>Words seem wholly inadequate, my friends. Why are the best books always the hardest to review?! Alas, if only I could have clever Lady Whistledown write this. <br/><br/>Flirtatious, affable, charming, and witty Colin has been my favorite Bridgerton sibling from the beginning,</span>
  <span id="freeText13939008361473153232" style="display:none"><i>Re-read/listened to the audiobook version Oct'2018</i>:<br><br>5 stars – Historical/Regency Romance<br><br>The audiobook narrator was fabulous, and it's still a big 5-star read for me.<br><br><i>Original Review from Sept'2010</i>: <br><br>5+ stars – Historical/Regency Romance <br><br>Words seem wholly inadequate, my friends. Why are the best books always the hardest to review?! Alas, if only I could have clever Lady Whistledown write this. <br><br>Flirtatious, affable, charming, and witty Colin has been my favorite Bridgerton sibling from the beginning, and I was most looking forward to his story, especially knowing that the strikingly handsome, popular bachelor was being paired with his sister’s sweet best friend, plump, unpopular, wallflower, spinster Penelope Featherington. I adore romances where the supposedly ugly duckling, Plain Jane heroine is finally seen as a beautiful swan, has her day in the sun, and finds happily ever after with the wonderful hero of her dreams, and <b>Romancing Mister Bridgerton</b> is one of the most enjoyable that I’ve read.<br><br>Colin and Penelope are perfect for each other, and the fact that they’re insecure, flawed, and have some growing up to do makes them all the more relatable and lovable. Their relationship progression, from friendship to love, was believable, sweet, and utterly romantic, and the love scene was exceptionally touching, beautiful, sensual, and tender. Colin’s gentle, passionate reverence of Penelope during their lovemaking was sigh-worthy.<br><br>It’s a heartwarming, funny, and delightful feel good romance with a swoon-worthy hero and an adorable heroine that will have you smiling, laughing, crying, cheering, sighing, and perhaps wishing for your very own Mr. Colin Bridgerton.<br><br>What else can I say? It’s like the highest quality dark chocolate...just scrumptious! I’m in love with Colin, I adore Penelope, and I simply love, love, <i>love</i> this book! 5 Big, dreamy stars!<br><br>My favorite Colin quote:<br><br><i>He murmured her name, tenderly taking her face in his hands. “I love you,” he said, his voice low and fervent. “I love you with everything I am, everything I’ve been, and everything I hope to be.”<br><br>“I love you with my past, and I love you for my future.” He bent forward and kissed her, once, softly, on the lips. “I love you for the children we’ll have and for the years we’ll have together. I love you for every one of my smiles, and even more, for every one of your smiles.”</i><br><br>I love that Colin has striking green eyes. How about Michael Vartan for Colin?<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380323086i/690530._SY540_.jpg" width="500" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><span>[image error]</span></span>

<div id="review_3606510646" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3606510646" />
    <a title="chan ☆" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48727754-chan"><img alt="chan ☆" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596680961p2/48727754.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3606510646?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chan ☆" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chan ☆" href="/user/show/48727754-chan">chan ☆</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3606510646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11973026841573666047"><b>not sure if it's the PMS or the book but i did release a singular bitch baby tear upon finishing this</b><br/><br/>i wasn't entirely enthusiastic about starting this fourth book because the first three books have been decidedly meh. <i>however,</i> julia quinn did a really good job setting up the relationship for this book at the end of the last one so i was a little more excited for this than i would have been otherwise. and honestly... this book didn't disappoint!<br/><br/>this was a childhood friends to lovers kind of stor</span>
  <span id="freeText11973026841573666047" style="display:none"><b>not sure if it's the PMS or the book but i did release a singular bitch baby tear upon finishing this</b><br /><br />i wasn't entirely enthusiastic about starting this fourth book because the first three books have been decidedly meh. <i>however,</i> julia quinn did a really good job setting up the relationship for this book at the end of the last one so i was a little more excited for this than i would have been otherwise. and honestly... this book didn't disappoint!<br /><br />this was a childhood friends to lovers kind of story. the hero and heroine weren't besties growing up but they definitely spent a lot of time together and that sort of made the heroine invisible to the hero for a while. watching him figure out what an absolute gem Penelope was, was such a treat.<br /><br />these are definitely my two favorite characters from the series so far and i was able to overlook a few things that annoyed me (but will mention here for y'all). i thought that Colin's hidden depths of being angry and jealous were not particular sexy. and the plot did meander a bit near the end. i understand that there can be multiple plot lines in a story but it felt like a little too much was going on at points. <br /><br />that being said, i really liked most of Colin &amp; Penelope's interactions. if you're looking for a pretty wholesome historical with a mostly non-douche hero &amp; a really cool and witty heroine i'd recommend this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11973026841573666047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer5314021719963499875">Meet Lady Whistledown, your one and only source into the scandalous lives of London's elite!<br/>I had high hopes for Colin's love story and the grand reveal of Lady Whistledown. Disappointment on both accounts. <br/>Colin is a shell of the man he used to be and there was no zing in his love story. He has also become somewhat of a jerk after all his globe trotting adventures. The only reason I didn't DNF this book was Penelope. I have a soft corner for wallflowers and Penelope seemed like a genuinely inte</span>
  <span id="freeText5314021719963499875" style="display:none">Meet Lady Whistledown, your one and only source into the scandalous lives of London's elite!<br />I had high hopes for Colin's love story and the grand reveal of Lady Whistledown. Disappointment on both accounts. <br />Colin is a shell of the man he used to be and there was no zing in his love story. He has also become somewhat of a jerk after all his globe trotting adventures. The only reason I didn't DNF this book was Penelope. I have a soft corner for wallflowers and Penelope seemed like a genuinely interesting character. Too bad her choice in men sucked. <br />This entire series (till this book, atleast) is pretty much like Gossip girl for peers, but with less sex and spice. I'm actually gonna take a break from the Bridgertons, go watch GG and fangirl over Nate (and his shoulders) for a while. XOXO.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6311119129045773969"><blockquote>
  <i>At some point in our lives we all ask some fundamental questions regarding our existence, the great mysteries of the universe, the past, the present and the future of humanity. Mankind is curious (and peculiar) like this; spending hours pondering on notions, dedicating personal effort and money, researching, reading, trying to find a solution to quench the hunger that consumes us. The Author knows this kind of struggle all too well. The last few days have been dedicated to the answer of one s</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText6311119129045773969" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>At some point in our lives we all ask some fundamental questions regarding our existence, the great mysteries of the universe, the past, the present and the future of humanity. Mankind is curious (and peculiar) like this; spending hours pondering on notions, dedicating personal effort and money, researching, reading, trying to find a solution to quench the hunger that consumes us. The Author knows this kind of struggle all too well. The last few days have been dedicated to the answer of one single question, one question to define her personality, her hopes, her dreams and wishes, but she still hasn't made up her mind. <br /><br /><b>Anthony or Colin Bridgerton?</b> <br /><br />How can a person choose? Anthony is the Rake turned into family man extraordinaire, while Colin is the carefree, smooth, genial and flirty gentleman every creature with ovaries adores, and thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110384.Romancing_Mister_Bridgerton__Bridgertons___4_" title="Romancing Mister Bridgerton (Bridgertons, #4) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Romancing Mister Bridgerton</a>, we discovered another side to him, that rendered him more alluring and, well,<b> delicious</b> (don't mind the Author, she's a notorious man-eater). The questionmark that haunts her thoughts may remain immoveable like the mountains, but the Author can declare with clarity that the forth story of the Bridgerton family is her <b>favorite</b>. She found a shadow of herself in Penelope Featherington, the witty, funny wallflower everyone overlooked. She devoured the pages (because aside from a maneater she's also a book-eater) that brought to life a <b>heart-warming</b>, <b>slow-burning</b>, <b>toe-curling</b> romance infused with the perfect dose of <b>hilarity</b> and <b>sensuality</b>, with spicy <b>scandals</b> and even spicier, clandestine meetings. And the cherry on top? <b>The bounty on Lady Whistledown's head</b>. Between precious Bridgertons' moments, falling in love and magical dances, the Author felt calm. At peace. Home. Penelope and Colin tugged at her heartstrings, and made her believe. <br />Believe that Colins Bridgerton exist.<br />(The Author is a little naive, so please forgive her extravagant declarations).<br /> <br />- Katerina's Bookish Papers, July 2018</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="6311119129045773969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_119800514" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119800514" />
    <a title="Jasmin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3284904-jasmin"><img alt="Jasmin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575041555p2/3284904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119800514?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmin" href="/user/show/3284904-jasmin">Jasmin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone looking for a sweet read ♥</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=reviewed-by-me">reviewed-by-me</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=humor">humor</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=aar-top-100-list">aar-top-100-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=must-read-series">must-read-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119800514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8912803352273490006"><blockquote>
  <i>”I am certainly not going to marry Penelope Featherington!”</i>
</blockquote><br/>Ever since we heard Colin Bridgerton <s>utter</s>, ummm, shout the above statement, we should have known that he’s going to eat his words sooner or later.<br/><br/>And eat them he did.<br/><br/>Penelope Featherington. She freshly comes out to society, out to meet the ton, with an excess of a few stones in her weight, and either orange/yellow/red gowns which doesn’t do her complexion any good. We can’t blame her. Her mother is a tyrant. But Penelope knows she d</span>
  <span id="freeText8912803352273490006" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>”I am certainly not going to marry Penelope Featherington!”</i>
</blockquote><br />Ever since we heard Colin Bridgerton <s>utter</s>, ummm, shout the above statement, we should have known that he’s going to eat his words sooner or later.<br /><br />And eat them he did.<br /><br />Penelope Featherington. She freshly comes out to society, out to meet the ton, with an excess of a few stones in her weight, and either orange/yellow/red gowns which doesn’t do her complexion any good. We can’t blame her. Her mother is a tyrant. But Penelope knows she doesn’t look good. The entire ton would agree with her. She also lacks the confidence to show her sharp wit to at least make up for her disgraceful attire. And instead of being seen as an intellectual lady with a terrible fashion sense, she’s seen as a stuttering plump and overripe orange, only worthy of staying at the sidelines as a wallflower. Season after season, she manages to improve herself, loosing the extra weight, however never being able to get rid of the horrendous clothes her mother has been forcing her, but still the ton doesn’t see her, or rather refuses to see her as her beautiful self. And she ends up on the spinster shelf.<br /><br />Colin Bridgerton. What more could he ask for? He’s loaded with good looks and charm. And he’s a Bridgerton. So, what more? Unfortunately, one does find it hard to seek contentment with just what he has. He has sought refuge in his travels. He’s not just the charming easygoing gentleman everyone thinks, because behind his beguiling smile are tons of layers of insecurities and dissatisfaction with his life.<br /><br />But in this work of fiction lies <b>real</b> people with <b>real</b> problems. How can we not relate to either one or both of them? Who hasn’t been insecure a few times in their life? Who hasn’t felt the fear of looking a fool? Who hasn’t dreaded no being able to search their life’s purpose?<br /><br />How could one not want what Penelope and Colin have? They were friends in the beginning and ended up as something more. And having one another seemed to be more than enough.<br /><br />Romancing Mr. Bridgerton, despite the laugh out loud parts and the easy smiles it caused me <i>or rather distressed me with, since I couldn’t help but smile in public places</i>, is a romance of tough and broad proportions. It made me laugh. It made me smile. It made me cry. It touched my heart and it touched my soul.<br /><br />And it also made me desire a certain Mr. Colin Bridgerton. He loves intensely. Just the way a certain me wants to be loved. As proof, I leave you with this:<br /><br /><blockquote><i>”I love you with everything I am, everything I’ve been, and everything I hope to be. I love you with my past, and I love you for my future. I love you for the children we’ll have and for the years we’ll have together. I love you for everyone of my smiles, and even more, for every one of your smiles.”</i>♥</blockquote><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8912803352273490006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lisa Kay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2459470-lisa-kay"><img alt="Lisa Kay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534570690p2/2459470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61115820?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Kay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Kay" href="/user/show/2459470-lisa-kay">Lisa Kay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/9138518-romancing-mister-bridgerton">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=genre-romance-historical">genre-romance-historical</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=theme-beauty-in-the-eye">theme-beauty-in-the-eye</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=character-bluestocking">character-bluestocking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=amazing-secondary-characters">amazing-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=m-pb-paperback">m-pb-paperback</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=authors-j">authors-j</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61115820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16423876941122184979"><i>St. Bride's Church Fleet Street, London, England, c.1830*</i><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379790354i/535361._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>★★★★½ I read this when it first came out over ten years ago and remember loving Colin. Though I’m a bit of a “re-reader,” I haven’t done so. Consequently, I jumped at the chance to join in a “buddy read,” the forth in this enduring series.<br/><br/>However, on re-read I was really impressed with Penelope. Don’t get me wrong: I still had heart palpitations over Colin and his deep green eyes. Nevertheless, I appreciated Penelope’s subtle straight-forw</span>
  <span id="freeText16423876941122184979" style="display:none"><i>St. Bride's Church Fleet Street, London, England, c.1830*</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379790354i/535361._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>★★★★½ I read this when it first came out over ten years ago and remember loving Colin. Though I’m a bit of a “re-reader,” I haven’t done so. Consequently, I jumped at the chance to join in a “buddy read,” the forth in this enduring series.<br><br>However, on re-read I was really impressed with Penelope. Don’t get me wrong: I still had heart palpitations over Colin and his deep green eyes. Nevertheless, I appreciated Penelope’s subtle straight-forward intelligence, calm humor, and not-so-common common sense. Not that she doesn’t have a secret or two up her sleeve. <br><br>I was also surprised at how much more I enjoyed seeing these two “perfect for each other” people – the wallflower spinster no one notices and the always popular “Golden Boy” – go from friendship to love on this second visit to Ms. Quinn’s world. <br><br>Of course, it isn’t strictly true that they were friends first, because Penelope has loved Colin for years. She always felt any attention Colin gave her was but perfunctory courtesy. Thus, it is a sweet delight to see him finally realize the jewel right under his nose. This story more than simply ‘holds up’ – it is definitely worthy of notice today.<br><br>P.S. I wish they’d put it on audio!<br><br>P.P.S. Ms Quinn borrowed the curmudgeonly** Lady Danbury from Stephanie Laurens’ <i>Cynster</i> series and made her more than a walk-on character – she’s an integral part of the plot. Such fun!<br><br>*19th century engraving; engraver unknown 19th century; public domain picture.<br><br>** Yes, I know “curmudgeonly” is a masculine term, but it works here, I think.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16423876941122184979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/760665654?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kinga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kinga" href="/user/show/110812-kinga">Kinga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780749936600" href="/book/show/1859053.Romancing_Mr_Bridgerton">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/110812-kinga?shelf=pub-2002">pub-2002</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer760665654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14373396608324116784">There is a perfect word to describe how I feel about Julia Quinn. It’s ‘meh’. I don’t love her, I don’t hate her, I will read her, I will quickly forget her.<br/><br/>I’m not sure why that is because she is very popular and other people seem to find her books, and this particular one especially, amazing. But to me they are just too cute. Too sweet. I don’t want cute and sweet. I’m sure you’ve gathered that much from my reviews – I can tolerate cute and sweet only in really homoeopathic doses.<br/><br/>So what is Ro</span>
  <span id="freeText14373396608324116784" style="display:none">There is a perfect word to describe how I feel about Julia Quinn. It’s ‘meh’. I don’t love her, I don’t hate her, I will read her, I will quickly forget her.<br /><br />I’m not sure why that is because she is very popular and other people seem to find her books, and this particular one especially, amazing. But to me they are just too cute. Too sweet. I don’t want cute and sweet. I’m sure you’ve gathered that much from my reviews – I can tolerate cute and sweet only in really homoeopathic doses.<br /><br />So what is Romancing Mr Bridgerton about? Well, she has loved him for ages, he barely notices her. Until he notices her and falls in love. And then they get married and live happily ever after. Also they make out in a carriage once which is something I have always wanted to do.<br /><br />The most interesting part of this story was how Quinn handled the bruised ego of the hero which was bruised on the account of his beloved being more successful than him (and what’s worse - in the same field!). This, I feel, needs to be addressed more often in romance novels. Is it unsexy for the hero to be less successful than the heroine? Especially if they work in the same field? Would you want to read a romance novel where a hero takes in his stride that he would never be as good of a scientist/doctor/writer as the heroine? How about real life? Personally, I prefer not to date another fiction writer just in case. Bruised male egos is something I have very little time for.<br /><br />*full reviews back to due to popular demand (true story)</span>

<div id="review_486835002" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/486835002" />
    <a title="LG (A Library Girl&#39;s Familiar Diversions)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14706534-lg-a-library-girl-s-familiar-diversions"><img alt="LG (A Library Girl&#39;s Familiar Diversions)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481347494p2/14706534.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/486835002?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LG (A Library Girl&#39;s Familiar Diversions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LG (A Library Girl&#39;s Familiar Diversions)" href="/user/show/14706534-lg-a-library-girl-s-familiar-diversions">LG (A Library Girl&#39;s Familiar Diversions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14706534-lg-a-library-girl-s-familiar-diversions?shelf=format-print">format-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14706534-lg-a-library-girl-s-familiar-diversions?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14706534-lg-a-library-girl-s-familiar-diversions?shelf=acquired-bought-used">acquired-bought-used</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14706534-lg-a-library-girl-s-familiar-diversions?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14706534-lg-a-library-girl-s-familiar-diversions?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer486835002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13261394834242292508">Oh, what a difference the second half of a book can make.<br/><br/>I want to be clear on this: when I was still only halfway through the book, I considered it a keeper. Penelope was wonderful: truly shy around anyone she didn't know well, with a few horribly painful/embarrassing moments in her life that Quinn actually took the time to show. I cringed in sympathy when Penelope came upon Colin just as he was telling his brothers that he wouldn't marry her and Penelope did what she could to preserve her dign</span>
  <span id="freeText13261394834242292508" style="display:none">Oh, what a difference the second half of a book can make.<br /><br />I want to be clear on this: when I was still only halfway through the book, I considered it a keeper. Penelope was wonderful: truly shy around anyone she didn't know well, with a few horribly painful/embarrassing moments in her life that Quinn actually took the time to show. I cringed in sympathy when Penelope came upon Colin just as he was telling his brothers that he wouldn't marry her and Penelope did what she could to preserve her dignity and not make it too obvious that he had just crushed her dreams. I enjoyed watching Penelope blossom as she resigned herself to being an old maid. Her friendship with Lady Danbury warmed my heart, and I loved it when they both confessed to attending horrible Smith-Smythe musicales so that the one Smith-Smythe girl who realized they were awful would have someone in the audience who was not making fun of her.<br /><br />I loved Colin, too. He was a nice guy, and never hurt Penelope on purpose. He felt miserable when she overheard him saying that he wouldn't marry her – it's just that he was too immature, at that point in his life, to know how to best handle the situation. Later on in their lives, when there was another moment when he could have accidentally hurt her feelings, she stopped him, and he took that time to think about the potential consequences of his actions and how Penelope might be hurt by them. Then he deliberately did his best not to hurt her. Colin wasn't in love with Penelope then and hadn't yet realized that a wonderful person had been right under his nose for years, but he still liked her, and I could have hugged him for the kind and thoughtful way he handled that moment.<br /><br />There's no way I can properly gripe about what Quinn did in the second half (last third?) of the book without spoiling things, so, if you don't like spoilers, stop reading this review at this point (or, more accurately, don't click the "spoiler" link).<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There are a few things I really hate coming across in romance novels. Widowed heroes or heroines still mourning the loss of their first spouses, babies and young children, very pregnant heroines, heroines whose physical description likens them to children, and...main characters who are writers. I've only encountered one author, Nora Roberts, who I can consistently trust to include any of these things without raising my hackles. <i>Romancing Mister Bridgerton</i> has shown me that I can't add Quinn to my short list.<br /><br />I was wondering where the book was going to go when, a little over halfway through it, Colin was already giddily insisting upon marrying Penelope and trying to get it through her mother's skull that, yes, he really did want to marry Penelope and not her sister Felicity. Then I found out, as Quinn revealed the big secret: Penelope is Lady Whistledown, the woman who had been anonymously skewering the ton for 11 years.<br /><br />I could have lived with this revelation (although I was annoyed that Quinn kept the reader in the dark via artificial means, by simply never having Penelope think about it). In fact, I enjoyed some of the angst that came from Penelope wondering if Colin was ashamed of her because of her work as Lady Whistledown. However, I felt that Lady Whistledown and writing in general then hijacked the story.<br /><br />This book has a grand total of one sex scene, which occurs prior to Colin and Penelope's marriage. They spend 70 pages of the book married – most authors would have found a way to fit a sex scene, even a fade to black one, in those 70 pages. I'm usually on the side of “more sweet romantic moments, less sex,” so I wouldn't necessarily have minded that Quinn only included one sex scene, if it weren't for the fact that it felt like there could, maybe should, have been one, and it was glossed over. Here is the moment when the book really made me angry:<br /><blockquote>“The wedding had been magical. It was a small affair, much to the dismay of London society. And the wedding night—well, that had been magical, too.<br /><br />And, in fact, marriage was magical, Colin was a wonderful husband—teasing, gentle, attentive...<br /><br />Except when the topic of Lady Whistledown arose.” (298)</blockquote><br />There were still 70 pages to go in the book. I had to reread the passage just to be sure that, yes, Quinn really had just glossed over Penelope and Colin's wedding, wedding night, and at least the first few days of their marriage...all because Lady Whistledown was suddenly the more important part of the book. Seriously??<br /><br />I finished the book because I do not DNF books when I'm that close to finishing them, but when I reached page 298 I decided that I could care less about all the Lady Whistledown stuff. I also began to find Colin's jealousy over Penelope being published (anonymously published, but still published) annoying. The writerly ego stroking scene that occurred when Colin finally let Penelope read his writings and she, of course, found them wonderful made me want to gag. That's probably a personal thing – I have a feeling that, if Colin had been worried about Penelope's reception of, say, his woodworking skills, I would have felt more sympathetic. Quinn just hit the wrong buttons with me when she made not one, but both her main characters writers, and then made that aspect an important part of the book. And, of course, Colin's writing was wonderful through and through – another thing that got my back up. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Others may not feel the same way about the ending that I did. However, because of that ending, a book I had initially considered a keeper is now one I'll be offloading in order to free up shelf space.<br /><br /><b>(Original review, with read-alikes and watch-alikes, posted on <a href="http://familiardiversions.blogspot.com/2011/12/romancing-mister-bridgerton-book-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">A Library Girl's Familiar Diversions</a>.)</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13261394834242292508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2137551144" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2137551144" />
    <a title="Ursula" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52878188-ursula"><img alt="Ursula" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499351015p2/52878188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2137551144?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ursula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ursula" href="/user/show/52878188-ursula">Ursula</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52878188-ursula?shelf=hero-is-an-arse">hero-is-an-arse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52878188-ursula?shelf=heroine-needs-a-backbone">heroine-needs-a-backbone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52878188-ursula?shelf=not-awful-but-not-great">not-awful-but-not-great</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52878188-ursula?shelf=not-my-cup-of-tea">not-my-cup-of-tea</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52878188-ursula?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52878188-ursula?shelf=heroine-deserves-better">heroine-deserves-better</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2137551144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14806528199219341543">BR with Andrea and Lacey. Thanks ladies- I am glad I read it. At least I am not dissing the book from a position of ignorance! It just is not my kind of romance:)<br/><br/>I had never liked the idea of this book, although I have read a few in this series and I seem to remember thinking they were ok. I could not enjoy this one.<br/>The writing was fine. It was both the MCs- they just plain annoyed me.<br/><br/>Colin was self-satisfied but insecure. He whined about having no purpose in his life, while he traveled the worl</span>
  <span id="freeText14806528199219341543" style="display:none">BR with Andrea and Lacey. Thanks ladies- I am glad I read it. At least I am not dissing the book from a position of ignorance! It just is not my kind of romance:)<br /><br />I had never liked the idea of this book, although I have read a few in this series and I seem to remember thinking they were ok. I could not enjoy this one.<br />The writing was fine. It was both the MCs- they just plain annoyed me.<br /><br />Colin was self-satisfied but insecure. He whined about having no purpose in his life, while he traveled the world having a good time. When he discovers our heroine's secret <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ she has published her writings <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> he is so jealous that he is cruel, even exhibiting quite bullying behaviour. (He actually pushes her around physically.) There is no discussion, no attempt to understand her point of view and no courage on his part to explain his aggressive and OTT reaction. He is constantly surprised that he could possibly be feeling anything for her- for God's sake, it was <i>Penelope Featherington</i>, after all. Plain, plump and old (28) Penelope. <br /><br />Penelope was a total doormat. Her mother pushed her around. The other debs pushed her around. Her bloody fiancé pushed her around. She is too busy saying sorry and trying to understand <b>their</b> point of view to ever realise that, hey, she has a right to do something worthwhile and creative with her own life. <br />She has a right to defend her position and decisions. <br />She has a right to say "no" to her mother. <br />She has a right to tell Colin he is way out of line and to pull his fucking head in. <br />But she was too sweet, too nice and too weak to assert herself at all. Not even once. Always quick with the backdown and full of mind numbing and cringe-worthy gratitude that Colin might actually want her- <b>Penelope Featherington</b>, <i>for God's sake!</i>.<br /><br />There were so many passages in the book that just made me angry. I should have highlighted them all and included them in this review, but it would have been pages long.<br />And I have a sneaking suspicion if the boot had been on the other foot, and Penelope had been the mean one, with poor Colin trying to justify a secret activity, all the HR fans out there would have been howling and calling her a nasty, spoilt, petulant cow. <br /><br />Even at the end, although we are given the sop that Penelope was his "editor", it is <i>Colin's</i> success that is lauded, <i>his</i> book she admires and <i>his</i> career that we are to look forward to. (She is preggo and that's her life over re: individual career or life purpose.) <br /><br />I do not like immature heroes and stereotypical, traditional roles in a relationship. That is not a true partnership. <br />Julia Quinn has definitely written some good books for me. This was absolutely <b>not</b> one of them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14806528199219341543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_70251263" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70251263" />
    <a title="Rane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1987431-rane"><img alt="Rane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419878997p2/1987431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70251263?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rane" href="/user/show/1987431-rane">Rane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=true-gem-keepers">true-gem-keepers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=regency-napoleonic-era">regency-napoleonic-era</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=keeper">keeper</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70251263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer608212690013314832"><i>Penelope Featherington has been in love with Colin Bridgerton for what seems like forever, from a young girl making her debut in society to a resign spinster. Penelope feelings have only grown throughout the years for Colin. Thinking she knew everything about Colin there was to know, Penelope comes across his hidden secret that starts to change her perspective of him in a surprising way that only draws them closer. <br/> Colin Bridgerton has always been the laid-back charmer of the family, but behind</i></span>
  <span id="freeText608212690013314832" style="display:none"><i>Penelope Featherington has been in love with Colin Bridgerton for what seems like forever, from a young girl making her debut in society to a resign spinster. Penelope feelings have only grown throughout the years for Colin. Thinking she knew everything about Colin there was to know, Penelope comes across his hidden secret that starts to change her perspective of him in a surprising way that only draws them closer. <br /> Colin Bridgerton has always been the laid-back charmer of the family, but behind the charmer mask lays a man looking for himself in the world, trying to make his mark, much like his brothers have done. When Penelope stumbles upon his secret he starts to see the young woman who’s always just been there in his life has changed into someone he truly never knew as she starts to haunt his thoughts and dreams.<br /> As both Colin and Penelope discover each other’s secrets, they start to see their true personality longing to break free and the deep love waiting for them both…</i><br /><br /><br /> There are few books I can say have hit a cord within me like Romancing Mister Bridgerton has. Penelope is one of those characters you can just step into their shoes and understand completely because you’ve been there, your felt what she felt, you know because you are her and she could have well been you. I related deeply with Penelope as she tells her story of being that wallflower on the fringes of the dance floor, in love with someone who didn’t even see her. Then becoming a spinster, because life didn’t give her just lemons, it only gave her an empty basket. Penelope never let it get her down, she did something with her life, and finally started to stand up to the world and be something she could never be : herself. She’s one of those strong characters who didn’t start off okay and got better; she started off great and only got greater. She was always this mature woman with a witty and sly humor whom was smart and very kind toward everyone and only became kinder, smarter as the story unfolds. <br /> <br /> I’ve always liked Colin and was looking forward to his story. After I finished, I love Colin. He showed something we all want to do in the world, find ourselves, leave our mark on the world, be something more. Colin did this with a few bumps in the road, but he did it. He archived his goal set before him, with the help of Penelope. I even understood his feelings of jealousy, his uneasiness with trying to go out on a limb and push his work out there for all to see. But he did something that made me love him, he became humble, he took a chance and reached out for help and support from Penelope. He became greater and I adored him for it. <br /><br /> The brightest moment was when Colin finally saw Penelope, saw her for her. I cried when he told her he loved her. Even when he showed his temper, he was showing a side he didn’t even know he had, a side of protectiveness and love. He didn’t say an empty sorry, he said it and backed it up. Penelope finally saw a side Colin that if possible made her love him even more. And their love scene was just so romantic, not hot and steamy, but soft and gentle, a true <b>love scene</b> that makes you wanna cuddle up to your love one. <br /><br /> It wouldn’t be a JQ book if there weren’t humor in it. The mystery behind whom Lady Whistledown is and the commotion it stirs within the ton, and the ever great Lady Danbury being the true scene stealer, but also showing a side never before seen by her. With the Bridgerton family always up to some sort of mischief or another that will always bring a smile to your face. RMB will have you reading the whole book, never wanting to put it down until the last page.(even loved the little tribute to Lisa Kleypas’s Dreaming of You) <br /><br /><b>Overall:</b> I’ll never be able to say enough great things about this book as it has becoming one of my all time favorite romances, but I’ll say this; it’s beautiful and wonderful, making you teary eyed when the shy wallflower blooms and finds her happy ever after with the man she loves and man whom loves her just as greatly!</span>
  <a data-text-id="608212690013314832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer368640967530614122"><b> 4.5 Danbury/Penelope stars </b><br/><br/>I absolutely love this series.<br/> Julia Quinn writes dialogue and wit better than most in this genre. <br/><br/>And upon my 3rd read... I still love Mrs Danbury and I still adore Penelope.<br/><br/> However, with each reading, Colin becomes increasingly unbearable. <br/>I cant think of any other book in which the heroine and a 70+ year old spinster steal the show while the hero is a bit of an insecure reflection of male mediocrity. <br/><br/>And even with this poor choice of gentleman, this book is a gem.</span>
  <span id="freeText368640967530614122" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 Danbury/Penelope stars </b><br /><br />I absolutely love this series.<br /> Julia Quinn writes dialogue and wit better than most in this genre. <br /><br />And upon my 3rd read... I still love Mrs Danbury and I still adore Penelope.<br /><br /> However, with each reading, Colin becomes increasingly unbearable. <br />I cant think of any other book in which the heroine and a 70+ year old spinster steal the show while the hero is a bit of an insecure reflection of male mediocrity. <br /><br />And even with this poor choice of gentleman, this book is a gem. Delightful fun. <br /><br /><i> Original review from 2014 below</i> <br /><br />4.5 Stars.<br /><br />I'd been looking forward to reading Colin's story, and it didn't disappoint. What's more, Penelope might be one of my more favourite heroines too, because of her subtle wit and strength, as opposed to some heroines who either lack these qualities or shove them down your throat.<br /><br />I also loved Lady Danbury.<br /><br />It lost half a star because I would have liked at least one more scene filled with flirtatious banter between the two main characters before they got engaged. It was all too sudden and too rushed. The proposal seemed to come out of nowhere and it was decidedly unromantic and an anticlimax. However, the scene where Colin visits Mrs Feathersby on a Monday afternoon has got to be one of the funniest scenes in the series so far, and had me giggle out loud (totally out of character for me).<br /><br />It is, all in all, a wonderful story about two people who've known one another since childhood. They eventually become friends, then confidantes, then lovers and finally soul mates.<br /><br />A great series and I've loved each book so far.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8655084-phrynne?shelf=5000-2019">5000-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2268964336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15741587560910960166">This series gradually works its way through the Bridgerton family, marrying one off in each book. This time it is the turn of Colin who we already know as the funny, charming, good looking one. Everyone loves Colin including Penelope who is a long time friend of the family. It is obvious from the start who is going to marry who but there are plenty of obstacles to overcome first.<br/><br/>I enjoyed the book very much as usual but must admit I struggled a little with its structure. Usually these books culm</span>
  <span id="freeText15741587560910960166" style="display:none">This series gradually works its way through the Bridgerton family, marrying one off in each book. This time it is the turn of Colin who we already know as the funny, charming, good looking one. Everyone loves Colin including Penelope who is a long time friend of the family. It is obvious from the start who is going to marry who but there are plenty of obstacles to overcome first.<br /><br />I enjoyed the book very much as usual but must admit I struggled a little with its structure. Usually these books culminate in the marriage. In this one the marriage took place just over half way through the book and was overwhelmed totally by other events. Then Colin seemed to suffer a personality transplant and became boorish and unpleasant and I felt disappointed on Penelope's behalf.<br /><br />Of course it all came good in the end. That's why we read romances isn't it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15741587560910960166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1970492298" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1970492298" />
    <a title="Caz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4368838-caz"><img alt="Caz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332962126p2/4368838.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1970492298?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caz" href="/user/show/4368838-caz">Caz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/34851677-romancing-mister-bridgerton">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=4-and-5-star-books">4-and-5-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=romance-1800-1850">romance-1800-1850</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1970492298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10251243736935613794">The friends-to-lovers trope is one of my favourites in the genre, and one of my favourite examples of it is Julia Quinn’s <strong>Romancing Mister Bridgerton</strong>, the fourth book in her iconic series about the eight Bridgerton siblings.<br/><br/>Colin is the third son, and has featured in the previous books as a good-humoured, devil-may-care sort of chap; easy going with a killer smile, good sense of humour, able to laugh at himself and always ready with a quip or witty rejoinder. He’s all of those things, but by the</span>
  <span id="freeText10251243736935613794" style="display:none">The friends-to-lovers trope is one of my favourites in the genre, and one of my favourite examples of it is Julia Quinn’s <strong>Romancing Mister Bridgerton</strong>, the fourth book in her iconic series about the eight Bridgerton siblings.<br /><br />Colin is the third son, and has featured in the previous books as a good-humoured, devil-may-care sort of chap; easy going with a killer smile, good sense of humour, able to laugh at himself and always ready with a quip or witty rejoinder. He’s all of those things, but by the age of thirty-three, has started to feel a little disgruntled at being thought of by practically everyone in society as just “A Bridgerton”. His brother is the viscount, his next eldest brother, Benedict, is making a name for himself as an artist but Colin… well, he’s not sure exactly what and who he is, and doesn’t quite know what he wants to do or to be, either.<br /><br />Penelope Featherington has also appeared in the previous books as a close friend of the Bridgerton sisters, especially of Eloise. She was an object of catty remarks and ridicule for years, owing to her mother’s tendency to dress her in styles and colours that were completely wrong for her and for that lady’s almost maniacal desire to get her daughters married off. At twenty-eight, Penelope is now firmly on the shelf and is resigned to being the spinster daughter who will care for her mother into old age – although the one good thing about her being on the shelf is that she can dress how she wants and eschew the horrible clothes her mother made her wear.<br /><br />Being a friend of the Bridgerton sisters means that Penelope has also been frequently in the company of the brothers, too, all of whom are friendly and treat her almost as one of the family, making a point of asking her to dance at balls or seeking her out at other functions. For years, Penelope has harboured a tendre for Colin, but has no hope of a return - why should he look at an unprepossessing woman like her when he’s one of society’s darlings; handsome, charming and witty, he is not without female admirers blessed with both youth and beauty and he can have any woman he wants.<br /><br />Ms. Quinn freshens up the trope and gives it extra depth by virtue of her characterisation of the two principals. Colin is restless; he travels a lot and in fact spends more time abroad than he does in England. He is tired of being thought of as someone who is only good for a laugh and wants to actually do something with his life but he has no idea what until one day, Penelope inadvertently stumbles upon one of his travel journals and is so engrossed by his writing that she suggests he publish them. At first, Colin is furious at her having read his private journals and they quarrel, but eventually, her genuine enthusiasm and praise for his writing surprise and humble him and start him thinking that perhaps this is what he’s meant to do, and he takes her suggestion to heart.<br /><br />Previously the perennial wallflower, Penelope has discovered that spinsterhood has its benefits; not only because she can dress as she wants, but because she feels free to be more herself and doesn’t have to put up with her mother’s constant attempts to marry her off. But Penelope has been keeping a huge secret from everyone around her for years; something that started as a way for her to fight back at those who looked down on her and that would ruin her if it ever got out. I’m not going to say more here because it’s a massive spoiler; but this secret is the book’s other major plotline and leads to some major conflict between Colin and Penelope later on.<br /><br />But the real strength of this instalment in the series is in the characterisation and subtle development of the two leads. Penelope’s infatuation with Colin is of long-standing; she fell for his looks and charm without really knowing him, and during the course of the story discovers that he’s not the perfect man she had imagined. Colin knows Penelope only as the slightly plump, shy friend of his sisters, but through spending time with her, comes to realise that she’s also intelligent, quick-witted and lovely. Neither of them really knows how or why things are changing between them, they just know that they <em>are</em>, and those moments when they both start to really see each other – the best parts of any friends-to-lovers romance - are beautifully done.<br /><br />Rosalyn Landor is, without question, one of the best narrators of historical romance around and her narrations of these previously unrecorded Bridgerton books (6, 7 and 8 were recorded some time ago, but not books 1-5) have been absolutely stellar. <strong>Romancing Mister Bridgerton</strong> is no exception; Ms. Landor’s pacing is excellent, her vocal characterisations of every single character are superb and in scenes where large numbers of characters appear, listeners can have no problems whatsoever working out who is speaking, so clear and expert is her manner of differentiating between all of them. It doesn’t matter if a character is old or young, male or female, aristocrat or servant, all are perfectly portrayed. I’m particularly fond of her interpretation of the formidable Lady Danbury, a wonderfully acerbic, perceptive but (secretly) kind elderly dowager of the sort so often found in historicals. Her portrayal of Colin, too, is spot on, and absolutely consistent with the way he was voiced in the earlier books in the series; suitably youthful and with a jaunty air that befits his reputation as a carefree young gentleman about town. But here, Ms. Landor is afforded the chance to explore another side of him, and she does it very well, adding a slight edge to his tone in some moments of heightened emotion or giving him a more seductive, husky note in the more intimate scenes.<br /><br />If you’re a fan of historical romance audiobooks, you’ve no doubt listened to Rosalyn Landor already and know that her name on the front cover is a guarantee of an excellent narration. If you haven’t tried one, then the <em><strong>Bridgerton</strong> </em>books can be listened to in any order, although I think you’ll get more out of them if you listen to them in order, as it will allow you to meet each sibling as they pop in and out of other stories in the series and get to know them better.<br /><br />Whatever you do, though, <strong>Romancing Mister Bridgerton</strong> is another must listen for fans of this talented author/narrator pair and for fans of historical romance in general.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10251243736935613794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1702804413" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1702804413" />
    <a title="Nadia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25547640-nadia"><img alt="Nadia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587020307p2/25547640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1702804413?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadia" href="/user/show/25547640-nadia">Nadia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25547640-nadia?shelf=could-ve-been-good-instead-it-s-meh">could-ve-been-good-instead-it-s-meh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1702804413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10018517642533724384">I don't know what's with me and Julia Quinn, but her books really don't work for me. I see that a lot of people love this series and her other books, I see that this book got a lot of love from readers, but I... I was bored most of the time. <br/><br/>Spoilers ahead.<br/><br/>Colin and Penelope were friends one moment and the other he wants to marry her. Just like that. I never saw how his feelings changed, we never witness his attraction, just all of a sudden they're kissing and he's asking her mother for her hand</span>
  <span id="freeText10018517642533724384" style="display:none">I don't know what's with me and Julia Quinn, but her books really don't work for me. I see that a lot of people love this series and her other books, I see that this book got a lot of love from readers, but I... I was bored most of the time. <br /><br />Spoilers ahead.<br /><br />Colin and Penelope were friends one moment and the other he wants to marry her. Just like that. I never saw how his feelings changed, we never witness his attraction, just all of a sudden they're kissing and he's asking her mother for her hand. <br /><br />And then the whole thing with Lady Whistledown. We find out about Penelope's secret life at the same time as Colin, and I wish we as readers were let in on the secret a bit earlier than that. I guess it would've brought a bit tension into this sugary honey sweet cotton candy chocolate-y story.<br /><br />And then there is the climax when Cressida blackmails Penelope because she somehow magically figured out that Penelope is Lady W. That's when Penelope was really stupid. Cressida had no prof to back up her claims, it was her word against Penelope's and Penelope could've easily played dumb and pretend she didn't know what Cressida was talking about. Like any normal person would do. Because this was a big secret and could ruin Penelope and whatever. But nooooo, she admits it almost right away and allows Cressida to blackmail her in her own house. And then Colin swoops in and lets the cat out of the bag in front of 500 people and everybody is happy they were being fooled and insulted and talked about for eleven years and we see that Colin and Penelope's fear of ruination was really unnecessary.<br /><br />I don't know, I'm the odd one here I guess. I don't know why I even try anymore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10018517642533724384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_864349336" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Joanna Loves Reading" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28993380-joanna-loves-reading"><img alt="Joanna Loves Reading" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509424316p2/28993380.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer6673201071395404233">I know this is an unpopular opinion, but this one is among my least favorite of the the series. I like Colin and Penelope separately as characters throughout the series. But their romance is rather blah. Colin acts like a man-child through most of this. Penelope never really had a shining moment that she owned. Ultimately I didn’t come away satisfied with the romance. Also, I think this second epilogue is not among the best.</span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review864349336">

<div id="review_3506446647" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3506446647" />
    <a title="Mo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11856352-mo"><img alt="Mo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1371247812p2/11856352.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3506446647?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mo" href="/user/show/11856352-mo">Mo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25573838-romancing-mister-bridgerton">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3506446647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17374515981728229624">4.5 sweet stars ...<br/><br/>Colin Bridgerton, the most charming man in London ... the most charming "single" man, maybe. I have a soft spot for his brother, Anthony (now married), the patriarch of the family ... I also have a soft spot for Simon (a brother in law) ... you know what? - all the Bridgertons are perfect!<br/><br/>This is the story of Colin and Penelope - Is Colin happy to continue his "man about town" lifestyle, is Penelope destined to be a spinster forever? <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1598253458i/30008292._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Everyone should read Historicals. I absolut</span>
  <span id="freeText17374515981728229624" style="display:none">4.5 sweet stars ...<br><br>Colin Bridgerton, the most charming man in London ... the most charming "single" man, maybe. I have a soft spot for his brother, Anthony (now married), the patriarch of the family ... I also have a soft spot for Simon (a brother in law) ... you know what? - all the Bridgertons are perfect!<br><br>This is the story of Colin and Penelope - Is Colin happy to continue his "man about town" lifestyle, is Penelope destined to be a spinster forever? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1598253458i/30008292._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Everyone should read Historicals. I absolutely adore them and I have to read one every so often. There are some good authors and there are some GREAT authors and I think Ms Quinn is a “great” author in this genre ...<br><br> <blockquote>
  <b>Colin Bridgerton was nice. Nice. Such a silly little word. It should have been banal, but somehow it fit him to perfection.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Yes, Colin was nice and lovely ... and, you know me, I usually shy away from the nice guys in books. Always like a bit of a cad or a rogue but there was something about Colin that was just "nice"! And Penelope was perfect for him ...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1598208003i/30006944.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>Isn't it nice to discover that we're not exactly what we thought we were?</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1598208003i/30006945._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <blockquote>
  <b>It was agony.<br>It was ecstasy.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Of course I love all the interactions with the Bridgerton siblings ... <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1598208181i/30006952._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <blockquote>
  <b></b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1598208003i/30006946._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <blockquote>
  <b>"They were never my dreams until I met you."</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1598208003i/30006947._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Swoon. Colin is just swoonworthy!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1598208003i/30006948._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And let's mention Lady Danbury ... great character.<br><br>The books are being serialised on Netflix in the near future. I was on Pinterest checking out some of the pictures ... Mmmm, not sure about the casting. I know when I read a book, I have an image in my head of someone but I shall reserve judgement until I see it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17374515981728229624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
