<div id="review_159894159" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159894159" />
    <a title="Carla *Jen7waters*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3288963-carla-jen7waters"><img alt="Carla *Jen7waters*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594777797p2/3288963.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159894159?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carla *Jen7waters*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carla *Jen7waters*" href="/user/show/3288963-carla-jen7waters">Carla *Jen7waters*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=2011-read">2011-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=nerdy-heroine">nerdy-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=favorite-heroines">favorite-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=heroine-v">heroine-v</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=unrequited-love">unrequited-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=ive-loved-you-since-4ever">ive-loved-you-since-4ever</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159894159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8085790859514929917"><s>Another favorite!</s> MY ABSOLUTE FAVORITE IN THE SERIES!<br/>Oh, this book made me so happy…<img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/95833.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Seriously, JULIA QUINN CAN DO NO WRONG.<br/><br/>Anyway, <b>Romancing Mister Bridgerton</b> is Colin’s book, and I almost couldn’t believe who's his lady in this... let your jaws drop fellow readers, for she is the plainest of Janes, wallflower of wallflowers, ugly duckling, the one and only: Miss Penelope Featherington! (MY GOD) And I love her so! Even in the previous books as a minor character - my heart would ache for that poo</span>
  <span id="freeText8085790859514929917" style="display:none"><s>Another favorite!</s> MY ABSOLUTE FAVORITE IN THE SERIES!<br>Oh, this book made me so happy…<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/95833.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seriously, JULIA QUINN CAN DO NO WRONG.<br><br>Anyway, <b>Romancing Mister Bridgerton</b> is Colin’s book, and I almost couldn’t believe who's his lady in this... let your jaws drop fellow readers, for she is the plainest of Janes, wallflower of wallflowers, ugly duckling, the one and only: Miss Penelope Featherington! (MY GOD) And I love her so! Even in the previous books as a minor character - my heart would ache for that poor girl always dressed in the wrong colors, with whom no one would dance except if their mamas told them to (tsk, tsk, Mr.Colin Bridgerton), and since that scene in <i>The Viscount Who Loved Me</i> when Anthony saves her from that awful-awful Cressida, I knew she ought to have her own book, so she could show them. Show every single one of those Bastards&amp;Co. who always rejected her and made fun of her, what she was made of. And she did! So my dear Penelope is now ahead of Sophie, my previous favorite-among-favorites Bridgerton series heroine. (Never fear Sophie, you're still in a solid number two.)<br><br>Colin and Penelope's love story is both heartbreaking and heartwarming -my favorite kind- mostly because she loves him since she first laid eyes on him, but he doesn't even dream of her in that way... until the day that he starts to. <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/167782.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>But until then Colin just 1.runs away -literally, and 2.messes things up when he's around, and oh boy... that atrocious scene from <i>An Offer From a Gentleman</i> when he shouts "I am certainly not going to marry Penelope Featherington!" with Penelope in the room...<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/168251.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Needless to say I got mad at him at the time for being a loud&amp;blind jackass, and got even madder at him now, for being a brute in a few occasions -when he didn't even had the right to- but he managed to redeem himself every time, so <i>I'm forgiving you</i> Mr. Bridgerton #3. But don't you dare act like an ass with Penelope ever again. Or else.<br><br>To the cast! This one is a bit difficult, but I'm saying:<br><br>Matt Dallas as Colin<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348146i/702425.jpg" width="230" height="284" alt="matt" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and Mandy Moore as Penelope<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348146i/702426.jpg" width="230" height="247" alt="mandy" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Too pretty? Maybe. But I think Mandy has the perfect tough cookie attitude to play Penelope. Plus, she really looks like the unpopular girl who could totally get the most desirable guy around. B-)<br><br>Oh! And there's a HUGE revelation in this book! All I can say about it is that, <i>I knew it! I knew it!</i> :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="8085790859514929917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/6972914-karen">Karen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2669770775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7560449392074676182"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547731143i/26930508._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Isn't it nice to discover that we're not exactly what we thought we were?</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>I really enjoyed this one. Loved Penelope and Colin. Thrilled that this feisty little wallflower finally got all she ever dreamed of. I hated that she'd had to feel passed over for most of her life. But sometimes the acceptance of one's ultimate fate, spinsterhood, can be quite a freeing experience. I wasn't sure how the author was going to finally bring these two together, especially after the things t</span>
  <span id="freeText7560449392074676182" style="display:none"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547731143i/26930508._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Isn't it nice to discover that we're not exactly what we thought we were?</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>I really enjoyed this one. Loved Penelope and Colin. Thrilled that this feisty little wallflower finally got all she ever dreamed of. I hated that she'd had to feel passed over for most of her life. But sometimes the acceptance of one's ultimate fate, spinsterhood, can be quite a freeing experience. I wasn't sure how the author was going to finally bring these two together, especially after the things that happened between them in the past, but in the end, I definitely think she pulled it off! <br><br>Moving on to Eloise... I've been dying to get to her book. :D</span>

<div id="review_138892371" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138892371" />
    <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog"><img alt="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352609417p2/2489554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138892371?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog">Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=drinks-on-me">drinks-on-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=king-of-the-harem">king-of-the-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=author-julia-quinn">author-julia-quinn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=genre-historical-romance">genre-historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=my-hottie-harem">my-hottie-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=the-hymen-club">the-hymen-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=books-i-go-rabid-over">books-i-go-rabid-over</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=series-bridgetons">series-bridgetons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138892371" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17725363531673614410"><b>Posted on <a href='http://underthecoversbookblog.blogspot.com/2012/02/review-romancing-mister-bridgerton-by.html' rel='nofollow noopener'></a> Under the Covers</b><br/><br/>Penelope Featherington has been overlooked her entire life. She’s been told that she’s not pretty enough, too plump, too nervous and too quiet. And yet, Penelope probably has the most personality out of all her heroines in this series. Penelope is hands down my favourite heroine! I love seeing her growth as a character in the previous ones leading up to her own book, Romancing Mr Bridgerton with her long-time crush, Colin.<br/><br/>I wondered how Colin would redeem himself after</span>
  <span id="freeText17725363531673614410" style="display:none"><b>Posted on <a href="http://underthecoversbookblog.blogspot.com/2012/02/review-romancing-mister-bridgerton-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener"></a> Under the Covers</b><br /><br />Penelope Featherington has been overlooked her entire life. She’s been told that she’s not pretty enough, too plump, too nervous and too quiet. And yet, Penelope probably has the most personality out of all her heroines in this series. Penelope is hands down my favourite heroine! I love seeing her growth as a character in the previous ones leading up to her own book, Romancing Mr Bridgerton with her long-time crush, Colin.<br /><br />I wondered how Colin would redeem himself after his flapping mouth exposed too much about how he felt about marrying Penelope in the last book. But even though Penelope was humiliated publicly by Colin’s outcry, she took it in stride, never letting Colin know how much it hurt her. <br /><br />Colin Bridgerton is the third son of the well-known family and he’s been portrayed as the devil-may-cry character. Colin is known for his easy smiles and his well-placed words, but in this book we discover that Colin has his unfulfilled fantasies and secret desires. Who would have suspected such a thing from Colin, who always seems to enjoy himself in everything?<br /><br />What I loved about this book is that we learn that there is more to the hero and heroine than we first thought. Quinn presents Penelope and Colin as one way, and in this book, we discover that there is more to these characters than we ever suspected.<br /><br />If you’ve been wondering who Lady Whistledown is, then rest easy because you do find out who it is in this one! I smacked my head when I found out! OF COURSE! I thought. It makes absolute perfect sense now that I look back. There were so many clues to indicate the true identity of the notorious Society paper queen.<br /><br />Also, if you’re read Lisa Kleypas’s Dreaming of You, then you may have noticed that Quinn incorporated one of Kleypas’s characters into this book. Penelope reads Mathilda by S.R. Fielding who is actually Sara, the heroine of the book! <br /><br />And of course, I have to talk about the romance between Penelope and Colin. While the previous book with Benedict was quick and passionate, Penelope and Colin’s romance was much slower and more solid. I love that Quinn makes each book different while still keeping it true to the characters. It makes each subsequent book entertaining to read. *sigh* I just adore this series!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17725363531673614410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300549321" />
    <a title="Exina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5309539-exina"><img alt="Exina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580809437p2/5309539.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300549321?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Exina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Exina" href="/user/show/5309539-exina">Exina</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=regency-romance">regency-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=m-f">m-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=great-writing-style">great-writing-style</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=london">london</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=likeable-heroine">likeable-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=great-characterization">great-characterization</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300549321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5026679137229753529"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/><b>Colin</b> is a sweet guy. He is always cheerful, always nice. He doesn't have dark secrets, or a tragic past, not even problems. Oh, wait, he has: he wants to leave something significant in the world. He is a talented writer, but he is too hesitant and shy, and he vacillates to publish his works. Is that really a serious problem?<br/>His character is too lightweight, he is too gentle, too sweet. He is even-tempered, and the one time he loses his head, even he is surprised by it.<br/><br/>But I loved <b>Penel</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5026679137229753529" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br /><b>Colin</b> is a sweet guy. He is always cheerful, always nice. He doesn't have dark secrets, or a tragic past, not even problems. Oh, wait, he has: he wants to leave something significant in the world. He is a talented writer, but he is too hesitant and shy, and he vacillates to publish his works. Is that really a serious problem?<br />His character is too lightweight, he is too gentle, too sweet. He is even-tempered, and the one time he loses his head, even he is surprised by it.<br /><br />But I loved <b>Penelope</b>. Her character is genuine and consistent. She is timid and reserved, but she can carry her point, and can be determinate. She is also very endearing, witty, and has an ironic sense of humor.<br /><br />The identity of <b>Lady Whistledown</b> is revealed in this book, but it is not as striking as I expected.<br /><br />Overall <i>Romancing Mr. Bridgerton</i> is an enjoyable romance, but the story and the characters (with the exception of Penelope) haven't left a deep impression on me.<br /><br /><br /><a href="http://exinasreadings.tumblr.com/tagged/Romancing-Mr-Bridgerton" rel="nofollow noopener">My favorite quotes.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5026679137229753529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2570485399" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2570485399" />
    <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt"><img alt="Jacob Proffitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325699498p2/1331641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2570485399?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Proffitt" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt">Jacob Proffitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25573838-romancing-mister-bridgerton">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=will-probably-regret">will-probably-regret</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2570485399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17793865663692420759"><em>This is fourth in a series and characters from the other three are important in this one. You can probably get by with simply knowing the relationships as presented here but I think it's worth knowing them in more detail from reading the other books. I wouldn't recommend skipping the first two, at any rate. The third isn't much present so skip that one if you like. Indeed, I urge you to—at least if you're likely to react as strongly negatively as I did.</em><br/><br/>I entered this with some trepidation becaus</span>
  <span id="freeText17793865663692420759" style="display:none"><em>This is fourth in a series and characters from the other three are important in this one. You can probably get by with simply knowing the relationships as presented here but I think it's worth knowing them in more detail from reading the other books. I wouldn't recommend skipping the first two, at any rate. The third isn't much present so skip that one if you like. Indeed, I urge you to—at least if you're likely to react as strongly negatively as I did.</em><br /><br />I entered this with some trepidation because I was so disappointed by the third book. And because I like Penelope and Colin so much from the previous books. I was particularly concerned about the long time jump (nine years?) between these books and the hint that we'd learn the identity of Lady Whistledown while we're at it made me hope that didn't turn out to suck. I needn't have worried as I think it turned out very well, though I have a major and a minor problem that keep this from being as good as it could have been.<br /><br />The major problem is that Quinn cheats and not in a small way. I'm not sure what she was thinking, but it was extremely cheap <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[to have Penelope's PoV not know that Penelope was Lady Whistledown. You read that right, there's a point where she asks herself, just to herself and all alone, things she'd have very well known being that <em>she actually is</em> Lady Whistledown. I wish I'd marked the spot so I could give detail because I was astonished how blatant it was. But because I'd guessed based on hints in the previous novels who it was I was watching for it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I'm not sure why Quinn did that. It didn't help the novel at all and I think the story would have been much better had she not gone to the ugly lengths she did.<br /><br />The minor issue was that I disliked Colin's angry/judgey bits. His reaction to learning things he doesn't like was to fly into a rage and it was so out of character I was shocked. And no, it doesn't help to have Quinn having him wonder at himself "this is so out of character for me." He recovers relatively quickly once he finally figures out why his reaction is so strong, but that still didn't reconcile me to his outbursty bits.<br /><br />Fortunately, Penelope was delightful and I loved her courage and willingness to put herself out there. Her emotional courage was outstanding and her support for Colin was remarkable, even in the face of his less noble actions. I liked that she recognized the harm of putting him so high on a pedestal and still loving him as she gets to know his less admirable doubts, fears, and emotional outbursts. And her support for publishing the journals from his travels was a lovely subplot that delighted me.<br /><br />Extending this, and solidifying my four-star rating, is that once they were together, they became a solid team and I loved that they communicated, even the hard bits. I loved that they came at their final challenge together and united and you could see that they would have done so even if they hadn't had the support of both the Bridgerton and Featherington clans. I don't for a minute buy the resolution as presented, people just aren't that eager to overcome resentments and slights, but by that time, I didn't care. Probably because I think they'd have been just as solidly triumphant even if the reaction had been diametrically opposite.<br /><br />So yeah, nice entry in the series and I'm so glad it worked out. This is my favorite of the series thus far and while I'll miss the Lady Whistledown sideplot, I'm glad it resolved so well.<br /><br /><strong>A note about Steamy</strong>: There's a single explicit sex scene but it's a long one. Still on the low end of my steam tolerance, though. Some of that is how well it fit the emotional and relationship character arcs and how it served to solidify my admiration of Penelope.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17793865663692420759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15045495758353265209">Penelope and Colin!   <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3231958421" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3231958421" />
    <a title="Radd Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17183363-radd-reader"><img alt="Radd Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536409036p2/17183363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3231958421?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Radd Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Radd Reader" href="/user/show/17183363-radd-reader">Radd Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25573838-romancing-mister-bridgerton">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17183363-radd-reader?shelf=guess-who">guess-who</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17183363-radd-reader?shelf=buddy-group-assigned-challenge">buddy-group-assigned-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17183363-radd-reader?shelf=favorite-couple">favorite-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17183363-radd-reader?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17183363-radd-reader?shelf=best-friends-sister-brother">best-friends-sister-brother</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3231958421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14064376697702510396"><b>
  <i>“Is life supposed to be this wonderful?”<br/>“I think so,” he murmured. “I really do.”<br/><br/>“I love you with everything I am, everything I’ve been, and everything I hope to be.”<br/><br/>“I love you. I adore you. I worship the ground you walk upon.”<br/></i>
</b><br/>London 1824<br/><i>
  <u>Characters</u>
</i><br/><u>Colin</u> (30, 3rd son of the Bridgerton family): <br/>The following words/phrases were used to describe hero: witty, dashing, devil-may-care jokester quality to him that made women swoon, nice, charmer, petulant, spoiled, unhappy, popular, confident, </span>
  <span id="freeText14064376697702510396" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“Is life supposed to be this wonderful?”<br />“I think so,” he murmured. “I really do.”<br /><br />“I love you with everything I am, everything I’ve been, and everything I hope to be.”<br /><br />“I love you. I adore you. I worship the ground you walk upon.”<br /></i>
</b><br />London 1824<br /><i>
  <u>Characters</u>
</i><br /><u>Colin</u> (30, 3rd son of the Bridgerton family): <br />The following words/phrases were used to describe hero: witty, dashing, devil-may-care jokester quality to him that made women swoon, nice, charmer, petulant, spoiled, unhappy, popular, confident, self-possessed, easy smile, devilish humor <br /><br />Three things about Colin:<br />- A little lost and dissatisfied with his life. With 2 older brothers who have found their place in the world, Colin is not quite sure where his path lies<br />- He writes about his travels, but he is insecure and vulnerable when it comes to the quality of his writing<br />- “haunted by unfulfilled dreams and secret insecurities.”<br /><br />Some quotes about Colin: <b>
  <i><br />“Every now and then, he simply had to get away. There was no other way to describe it.<br />Away from the ton, who thought him a charming rogue and nothing else, away from England, which encouraged younger sons to enter the military or the clergy, neither of which suited his temperament. Even away from his family, who loved him unconditionally but had no clue that what he really wanted, deep down inside, was something to do.”<br /><br />“He wanted a purpose.<br />He wanted a legacy.”<br /><br />“there was something about Colin that set everyone at ease.”<br /><br />“It’s clear that your travels feed your soul.”<br /><br />“Colin was coming to think that perhaps being well liked was over-rated. Heaven knew that no one was better liked than he was, and look at him now, frustrated and malcontent, grumpy and ready to lash out at anyone who crossed his path.”<br /></i>
</b><br /><u>Penelope (28)</u>: <br />The following words/phrases were used to describe Penelope: cheeky, smart, kind, funny, surprising, dry wit, sly smile, intelligent mind, glowing, siren, goddess, lovely, clever, enchanting<br /><br />Three things about Penelope:<br />- Her BFF is Eloise Bridgerton (Colin’s younger sister)<br />- She considers herself an on-the-shelf spinster and doesn’t see how that will change<br />- She has been in love with Colin Bridgerton for the last 10 years<br /><br />Some quotes about Penelope: <b>
  <i><br />“Deep inside, she knew who she was, and that person was smart and kind and often even funny, but somehow her personality always got lost somewhere between her heart and her mouth, and she found herself saying the wrong thing or, more often, nothing at all.”<br /><br />“Miss Penelope Featherington’s unfortunate gown left the unfortunate girl looking like nothing more than an overripe citrus fruit.”<br /><br />“She had to go and fall in love with Colin Bridgerton when he fell off a horse and landed on his bottom in a mud puddle.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><u>My Thoughts:</u><br />The following are my thoughts about this book: <br />- Penelope’s long-standing crush on Colin was palpable....she had it bad for him 😍<i>“This was love. Oh, this was love love love love love love. A silly repetition of words, perhaps, but that was precisely what Penelope doodled on a ridiculously expensive sheet of writing paper, along with the words, “Mrs. Colin Bridgerton” and “Penelope Bridgerton” and “Colin Colin Colin.”</i>😍<br />- Lady Whistledown reveal 👍👏👏🤩. Woot Woot!!<br />- Colin was downright swoon-worthy 🥰🥰<br />- I loved Penelope. Deep down she was such a strong woman. <br />- I was so happy that Penelope didn’t keep the blackmail incident to herself and immediately told Colin. Kudos to the author for not succumbing to the over-used plot device of miscommunication and secrets just to cause conflict within a story. I loved that they talked about it and tossed around solutions together. 👍👍<br />- I liked that Colin and Penelope both had insecurities and that ultimately they offered the encouragement and support that the other person needed. They made a good team. <br />- I liked the growth the two characters showed throughout the story. <br />- This was my favorite Bridgerton book so far. <br /><br /><u>Recap: </u><br />- <i>Do you need to read previous books in series?:</i> it would probably help, but not completely necessary. This couple is front and center to the story and anyone from a previous book is in the background. However, to fully understand the Lady Whistledown aspect, you might want to read other books first. <br />- <i>POV:</i> dual POV<br />- <i>Tropes:</i> best friend’s brother, unrequited love, friends to lovers<br />- <i>H likable?</i> Yes. Swoony 😍<br />- <i>h likable?</i> Yes. I loved her<br />- <i>h virgin?</i> yes<br />- <i>First time they kiss:</i> 36%<br />- <i>First time they sleep together:</i> 77%<br />- <i>steamy?</i> not especially. They have chemistry, but it’s not overly steamy<br />- <i>OW/OM drama?</i> no<br />- <i>H/h cheat?</i> no<br />- <i>Did I skip pages?</i> No<br />- <i>Big secrets?</i> yes. The secret was revealed at 52%<br />- <i>Did I cry?</i> no<br />- <i>Did I laugh? </i> no<br />- <i>Cliffhanger?</i> no<br />- <i>Epilogue?</i> 1 year later<br />- <i>Recommend?</i> yes<br /><br /><u>Quotes</u><i><br />“She’s lost nearly two stone and could now call herself “pleasantly rounded” rather than “a hideous pudge.”<br /><br />“Good heavens,” she moaned. If sin could take a solid form, surely it would be a pastry. Preferably one with chocolate.”<br /><br />“There wasn’t a woman alive who could go from point A to B without stopping at C, D, X, and 12 along the way.”<br /><br />“Next time you want to complain about the trials and tribulations of universal adoration, try being an on-the-shelf spinster for a day. See how that feels and then let me know what you want to complain about.”<br /><br />“Colin was still sprawled on the sofa, gaping at her as if she were some bizarre creature with three heads, twelve fingers, and a tail,”<br /><br />“Now, will you just tell me what is wrong, or do you plan to wait until I expire of impatience?”<br /><br />“Maybe this, then, was the definition of love. When you wanted someone, needed her, adored her still, even when you were utterly furious and quite ready to tie her to the bed just to keep her from going out and making more trouble.”<br /><br />“I love you with my past, and I love you for my future.” He bent forward and kissed her, once, softly, on the lips. “I love you for the children we’ll have and for the years we’ll have together. I love you for every one of my smiles, and even more, for every one of your smiles.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14064376697702510396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jHKPZNTcNFW6MijQqDKzTwyN3coIXXLP7a9ghffW5+G2taLHBEN+UDuItZDov8laI2mSkdOg+ZTRmsqI7CdROA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pbFfZpWZY3w9ZaOY1AWd3dZOReOK5UMxV3BfOkkSqNyfdnLFRQYpebzfPtiUiOfI+aoKuFEYyGprRfU3UuMeBQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer11080730621628592183">#1 New York Times bestselling author Julia Quinn loves to dispel the myth that smart women don't read (or write) romance, and and if you watch reruns of the game show The Weakest Link you might just catch her winning the $79,000 jackpot. She displayed a decided lack of knowledge about baseball, country music, and plush toys, but she is proud to say that she aced all things British and literary, an</span>
  <span id="freeText11080730621628592183" style="display:none">#1 New York Times bestselling author Julia Quinn loves to dispel the myth that smart women don't read (or write) romance, and and if you watch reruns of the game show The Weakest Link you might just catch her winning the $79,000 jackpot. She displayed a decided lack of knowledge about baseball, country music, and plush toys, but she is proud to say that she aced all things British and literary, answered all of her history and geography questions correctly, and knew that there was a Da Vinci long before there was a code.<br /><br />A graduate of Harvard and Radcliffe Colleges, Ms. Quinn is one of only sixteen members of Romance Writers of America’s Hall of Fame. Her books have been translated into 32 languages, and she lives with her family in the Pacific Northwest.<br /><br />The Bridgertons, her popular series of historical romance, is currently in production by Shondaland as a Netflix original series starring Julie Andrews, Phoebe Dynevor, and Rége-Jean Page.</span>

From their earliest days, children of aristocrats learn how to address an earl and curtsey before a prince—while other dictates of the ton are unspoken yet universally understood. A proper duke should be imperious and aloof. A young, marriageable lady should be amiable…but not too amiable.\n\nDaphne Bridgerton has always failed at the latter. The fourth of eight siblings in her close-knit family, she has formed friendships with the most eligible young men in London. Everyone likes Daphne for her kindness and wit. But no one truly desires her. She is simply too deuced honest for that, too unwilling to play the romantic games that captivate gentlemen.\n\nAmiability is not a characteristic shared by Simon Basset, Duke of Hastings. Recently returned to England from abroad, he intends to shun both marriage and society—just as his callous father shunned Simon throughout his painful childhood. Yet an encounter with his best friend’s sister offers another option. If Daphne agrees to a fake courtship, Simon can deter the mamas who parade their daughters before him. Daphne, meanwhile, will see her prospects and her reputation soar.\n\nThe plan works like a charm—at first.
